## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and concentration A, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics — determining the rate law from kinetic data.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, first-order decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate expression)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions with equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Competitive inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (competitive product inhibition)
- Time-dependent forcing with decay: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * A (externally driven reaction)
- Combined order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**c2 (surface-catalyzed reaction)
- Sigmoidal rate: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative kinetics, Hill equation)
- Damped oscillatory input: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodic forcing on reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservation constraints: If A is part of a closed system (A + B = const), the rate law in A alone may appear as polynomial with both positive and negative terms, e.g., A*(c-A)
- Equilibrium approach: A nonzero constant term added to a linear-in-A rate law (c0*A + c1) indicates a reversible reaction approaching equilibrium
- Enzyme saturation: When rate increases linearly at low A but plateaus at high A, use rational forms A/(c+A) characteristic of Michaelis-Menten mechanisms
- Cooperative binding: Hill-type expressions A^n/(c+A^n) with n>1 indicate cooperative or allosteric effects in biochemical kinetics
- Sequential mechanism signatures: Products of concentration terms like A^m * (c-A)^n arise from coupled sequential or parallel reaction steps
- Catalytic surface reactions: Denominators with (1+c*A)^2 indicate dual-site Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanisms on catalytic surfaces
- Induction periods: Explicit time dependence multiplied by concentration terms (e.g., t*A or exp(-c*t)*A) suggests initiation/induction phenomena
- Negative fractional orders: Rate expressions with A**c where 0<c<1 suggest diffusion-limited or fractal kinetics rather than elementary reactions

**Candidate 78:** Set c2=0, c5=0 → `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c1`. **MATCH**

**Candidate 79:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c1 + A^c2*c3 + c4`. Set c3=0, c4=0 → match. **MATCH**

**Candidate 80:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c1 + c2*t/(c3*t+c4) + c5/(c3*t+c4)`. Set c2=0, c5=0 → match. **MATCH**

**Candidate 81:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c1 + c2*t*(A+c3)^c4`. Set c2=0 → match. **MATCH**

**Candidate 82:** `A^(1/3)*c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + A*c3 + A*c4/(A+c5) + c6`. The A^(1/3) term has t-dependence through sin. Set c0=0 → `A*c3 + A*c4/(A+c5) + c6`. This is rational in A, can't produce A^(1/3). So we need c0≠0, but then sin(c1*t+c2) makes it t-dependent unless c1=0. Set c1=0 → `A^(1/3)*c0*sin(c2) + A*c3 + A*c4/(A+c5) + c6`. sin(c2) is just a constant, absorbed into c0. Set c4=0, c6=0 → `A^(1/3)*c0' + A*c3`. **MATCH**

**Candidate 83:** `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + A^c2*c3*exp(c4*t)`. Set c1=0, c4=0 → `A*c0 + c3*A^c2`. Set c2=1/3. **MATCH**

**Candidate 84:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c1 + c2*t^c3`. Set c2=0 → match. **MATCH**

**Candidate 85:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*t^c3`. Set c2=0 → match. **MATCH**

**Candidate 86:** `A^(1/3)*c0*exp(c1*t) + A*c2 + A*c3/(A+c4) + c5`. Set c1=0, c3=0, c5=0 → `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c2`. **MATCH**

**Candidate 87:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + c3*exp(c4*t) + c5`. Set c3=0, c5=0, c1=1/3 → match. **MATCH**

**Candidate 88:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c1 + c2*exp(c3*t)`. Set c2=0 → match. **MATCH**

**Candidate 89:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2*exp(c3*t)`. Set c2=0 → match. **MATCH**

**Candidate 90:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4 + c5*log(A*c6+1)`. Set c3=0, c4=0, c5=0 → `A*c0 + c2*A^c1`. Set c1=1/3. **MATCH**

**Candidate 91:** `A*c0 + A*c1/(A+c2) + A^c3*c4/(A^c3+c5) + c6`. Set c1=0, c6=0: `A*c0 + c4*A^c3/(A^c3+c5)`. The second term is bounded (approaches c4 as A→∞), can't produce A^(1/3). Set c5=0 → `A*c0 + c4`. Constant + linear. Set c4=0 → `A*c0 + A*c1/(A+c2) + c6`. Rational, can't produce A^(1/3). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 92:** `A^2*c0 + A*c1 + A^c2*c3/(A^c2+c4) + c5`. Set c4=0 → `A^2*c0 + A*c1 + c3 + c5`. Set c0=0 → `A*c1 + c3+c5`. No A^(1/3). Set c0=0, c5=0: `A*c1 + c3*A^c2/(A^c2+c4)`. The fraction is bounded. Can't produce A^(1/3). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 93:** `A^c0*c1*(-A+c2)^c3 + A^c4*c5*exp(c6*t)`. Set c6=0, c3=0 → `c1*A^c0 + c5*A^c4`. Set c0=1/3, c4=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 94:** `A^c0*c1 + A^c2*c3*sin(c4*t+c5) + c6`. Set c4=0 → `A^c0*c1 + c3*sin(c5)*A^c2 + c6`. Set c6=0, c0=1/3, c2=1. **MATCH**

**Candidate 95:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*exp(c5*t) + c6`. Set c3=0, c4=0, c6=0 → `A*c0 + c2*A^c1`. Set c1=1/3. **MATCH**

**Candidate 96:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2*log(A*c3+1) + c4`. Set c2=0, c4=0 → `A*c0`. Missing A^(1/3). log can't produce A^(1/3). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 97:** `A^c0*c1 + c2 + c3*log(A^c4*c5+1)`. Set c3=0, c2=0 → `c1*A^c0`. Single power. Can't get two powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 98:** `A^2*c0 + A*c1 + c2 + c3*exp(A^c4*c5)`. Set c3=0, c0=0, c2=0 → `A*c1`. Missing A^(1/3). exp can't produce it. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 99:** `A*c0/(A*c1+c2) + A^c3*c4 + c5 + c6/(A*c1+c2)`. Set c0=0, c6=0, c5=0 → `c4*A^c3`. Single power. Keep c0,c6: `(A*c0+c6)/(A*c1+c2) + c4*A^c3 + c5`. The fraction is rational (approaches c0/c1), can't produce A^(1/3). Set c3=1/3, c5=0: `(A*c0+c6)/(A*c1+c2) + c4*A^(1/3)`. The fraction → c0/c1 as A→∞ but GT has no constant. Set c1=0: `(A*c0+c6)/c2 + c4*A^(1/3)` = `(c0/c2)*A + c6/c2 + c4*A^(1/3)`. Set c6=0 → `(c0/c2)*A + c4*A^(1/3)`. **MATCH**

**Candidate 100:** `A^c0*c1 + c2 + c3*exp(A^(1/3)*c4)`. Set c3=0, c2=0 → single power. Need two. Set c4=0 → `c1*A^c0 + c2 + c3`. Set c2+c3=0, c0=1 → `c1*A`. Missing A^(1/3). Set c0=1/3 → `c1*A^(1/3)`. Missing A. Can't get both. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 101:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2/(A^c1+c3) + c4`. The fraction A^c1*c2/(A^c1+c3) is bounded (→c2 as A→∞). Can't produce A^(1/3) growth. Set c3=0 → `A*c0 + c2 + c4`. No A^(1/3). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 102:** `A^c0*c1 + A^c2*c3/(A^c2+c4) + c5`. Set c4=0 → `c1*A^c0 + c3 + c5`. Single power + constant. Set c5+c3=0 → `c1*A^c0`. Single power. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 103:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2/(A^c1+c3) + c4*exp(c5*t) + c6`. Set c4=0, c3=0 → `A*c0 + c2 + c6`. No A^(1/3). Bounded fraction. **NO MATCH**
